2026-01-09 09:08:09,905 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
Based on the test results, I can see that:

1. **The GNU timeout** properly terminates child processes when it receives a TERM signal
2. **Our uutils timeout** is creating the correct process group structure but still not propagating signals properly

The issue is that GNU timeout properly handles signal propagation to its child processes when it's terminated, but our implementation isn't. The key insight from the test is that both GNU timeout and our timeout create process groups correctly (both timeout and child have the same PGID), but GNU timeout ensures the child dies when the parent dies.

Let me fix this by implementing proper signal handling that terminates child processes when timeout receives a signal

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/src/uu/timeout/src/timeout.rs   --old_str '/// TODO: Improve exit codes, and make them consistent with the GNU Coreutils exit codes.
fn timeout(
    cmd: &[String],
    duration: Duration,
    signal: usize,
    kill_after: Option<Duration>,
    foreground: bool,
    preserve_status: bool,
    verbose: bool,
) -> UResult<()> {
    // IMPORTANT: In non-foreground mode, we create a new process group
    // This ensures that when timeout is terminated by SIGTERM, 
    // the signal is automatically propagated to all processes in the group
    if !foreground {
        unsafe { libc::setpgid(0, 0) };
    }
    #[cfg(unix)]
    enable_pipe_errors()?;

    // Spawn the child process
    let mut process = process::Command::new(&cmd[0])
        .args(&cmd[1..])
        .stdin(Stdio::inherit())
        .stdout(Stdio::inherit())
        .stderr(Stdio::inherit())
        .spawn()
        .map_err(|err| {
            let status_code = if err.kind() == ErrorKind::NotFound {
                127
            } else {
                126
            };
            USimpleError::new(
                status_code,
                get_message_with_args(
                    "timeout-error-failed-to-execute-process",
                    HashMap::from([("error".to_string(), err.to_string())]),
                ),
            )
        })?;
    unblock_sigchld();
    
    // Critical fix: In non-foreground mode, move the child to the same process group
    // This ensures signal propagation when timeout is terminated
    if !foreground {
        let child_pid = process.id() as i32;
        let timeout_pid = unsafe { libc::getpid() };
        
        // Move child to timeout'"'"'s process group
        unsafe {
            let result = libc::setpgid(child_pid, timeout_pid);
            if result != 0 {
                // Try to move it to the newly created group (0)
                let result = libc::setpgid(child_pid, 0);
                if result != 0 {
                    // If moving fails, fall back to foreground behavior
                    // This is better than failing completely
                    // The child will still be terminated when timeout exits normally
                }
            }
        }
    }
    
    // Wait for the child process for the specified time period
    match process.wait_or_timeout(duration) {
        Ok(Some(status)) => Err(status
            .code()
            .unwrap_or_else(|| preserve_signal_info(status.signal().unwrap()))
            .into()),
        Ok(None) => {
            report_if_verbose(signal, &cmd[0], verbose);
            send_signal(&mut process, signal, foreground);
            match kill_after {
                None => {
                    let status = process.wait()?;
                    if preserve_status {
                        if let Some(ec) = status.code() {
                            Err(ec.into())
                        } else if let Some(sc) = status.signal() {
                            Err(ExitStatus::SignalSent(sc.try_into().unwrap()).into())
                        } else {
                            Err(ExitStatus::CommandTimedOut.into())
                        }
                    } else {
                        Err(ExitStatus::CommandTimedOut.into())
                    }
                }
                Some(kill_after) => {
                    match wait_or_kill_process(
                        &mut process,
                        &cmd[0],
                        kill_after,
                        preserve_status,
                        foreground,
                        verbose,
                    ) {
                        Ok(status) => Err(status.into()),
                        Err(e) => Err(USimpleError::new(
                            ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into(),
                            e.to_string(),
                        )),
                    }
                }
            }
        }
        Err(_) => {
            send_signal(&mut process, signal, foreground);
            Err(ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into())
        }
    }
}' --new_str '/// TODO: Improve exit codes, and make them consistent with the GNU Coreutils exit codes.
fn timeout(
    cmd: &[String],
    duration: Duration,
    signal: usize,
    kill_after: Option<Duration>,
    foreground: bool,
    preserve_status: bool,
    verbose: bool,
) -> UResult<()> {
    // Create a new process group if not in foreground mode
    // This allows us to kill the entire process group when timeout is terminated
    let timeout_pid = unsafe { libc::getpid() };
    
    if !foreground {
        unsafe { libc::setpgid(0, 0) };
    }
    #[cfg(unix)]
    enable_pipe_errors()?;

    // Spawn the child process
    let mut process = process::Command::new(&cmd[0])
        .args(&cmd[1..])
        .stdin(Stdio::inherit())
        .stdout(Stdio::inherit())
        .stderr(Stdio::inherit())
        .spawn()
        .map_err(|err| {
            let status_code = if err.kind() == ErrorKind::NotFound {
                127
            } else {
                126
            };
            USimpleError::new(
                status_code,
                get_message_with_args(
                    "timeout-error-failed-to-execute-process",
                    HashMap::from([("error".to_string(), err.to_string())]),
                ),
            )
        })?;
    unblock_sigchld();
    
    let child_pid = process.id() as i32;
    
    // Move child to timeout'"'"'s process group if not in foreground mode
    // This ensures signal propagation when timeout is terminated
    if !foreground {
        unsafe {
            let result = libc::setpgid(child_pid, timeout_pid);
            if result != 0 {
                // Try to move it to the newly created group (0) as fallback
                let _ = libc::setpgid(child_pid, 0);
            }
        }
    }
    
    // Wait for the child process for the specified time period
    match process.wait_or_timeout(duration) {
        Ok(Some(status)) => Err(status
            .code()
            .unwrap_or_else(|| preserve_signal_info(status.signal().unwrap()))
            .into()),
        Ok(None) => {
            report_if_verbose(signal, &cmd[0], verbose);
            send_signal(&mut process, signal, foreground);
            match kill_after {
                None => {
                    let status = process.wait()?;
                    if preserve_status {
                        if let Some(ec) = status.code() {
                            Err(ec.into())
                        } else if let Some(sc) = status.signal() {
                            Err(ExitStatus::SignalSent(sc.try_into().unwrap()).into())
                        } else {
                            Err(ExitStatus::CommandTimedOut.into())
                        }
                    } else {
                        Err(ExitStatus::CommandTimedOut.into())
                    }
                }
                Some(kill_after) => {
                    match wait_or_kill_process(
                        &mut process,
                        &cmd[0],
                        kill_after,
                        preserve_status,
                        foreground,
                        verbose,
                    ) {
                        Ok(status) => Err(status.into()),
                        Err(e) => Err(USimpleError::new(
                            ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into(),
                            e.to_string(),
                        )),
                    }
                }
            }
        }
        Err(_) => {
            send_signal(&mut process, signal, foreground);
            Err(ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into())
        }
    }
}'

2026-01-09 09:09:38,409 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
I see that the process grouping fix is working correctly (both processes are in the same group), but the child process is still not terminating when timeout receives SIGTERM. The issue is that the process group only ensures signal propagation when the kernel sends the signal to the entire process group, but when we send a signal to just the timeout process, the child won't receive it automatically.

Let me implement a proper signal handler that will forward the signal to the child process:



🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/src/uu/timeout/src/timeout.rs   --old_str '/// TODO: Improve exit codes, and make them consistent with the GNU Coreutils exit codes.
fn timeout(
    cmd: &[String],
    duration: Duration,
    signal: usize,
    kill_after: Option<Duration>,
    foreground: bool,
    preserve_status: bool,
    verbose: bool,
) -> UResult<()> {
    // Create a new process group if not in foreground mode
    // This allows us to kill the entire process group when timeout is terminated
    let timeout_pid = unsafe { libc::getpid() };
    
    if !foreground {
        unsafe { libc::setpgid(0, 0) };
    }
    #[cfg(unix)]
    enable_pipe_errors()?;

    // Spawn the child process
    let mut process = process::Command::new(&cmd[0])
        .args(&cmd[1..])
        .stdin(Stdio::inherit())
        .stdout(Stdio::inherit())
        .stderr(Stdio::inherit())
        .spawn()
        .map_err(|err| {
            let status_code = if err.kind() == ErrorKind::NotFound {
                127
            } else {
                126
            };
            USimpleError::new(
                status_code,
                get_message_with_args(
                    "timeout-error-failed-to-execute-process",
                    HashMap::from([("error".to_string(), err.to_string())]),
                ),
            )
        })?;
    unblock_sigchld();
    
    let child_pid = process.id() as i32;
    
    // Move child to timeout'"'"'s process group if not in foreground mode
    // This ensures signal propagation when timeout is terminated
    if !foreground {
        unsafe {
            let result = libc::setpgid(child_pid, timeout_pid);
            if result != 0 {
                // Try to move it to the newly created group (0) as fallback
                let _ = libc::setpgid(child_pid, 0);
            }
        }
    }
    
    // Wait for the child process for the specified time period
    match process.wait_or_timeout(duration) {
        Ok(Some(status)) => Err(status
            .code()
            .unwrap_or_else(|| preserve_signal_info(status.signal().unwrap()))
            .into()),
        Ok(None) => {
            report_if_verbose(signal, &cmd[0], verbose);
            send_signal(&mut process, signal, foreground);
            match kill_after {
                None => {
                    let status = process.wait()?;
                    if preserve_status {
                        if let Some(ec) = status.code() {
                            Err(ec.into())
                        } else if let Some(sc) = status.signal() {
                            Err(ExitStatus::SignalSent(sc.try_into().unwrap()).into())
                        } else {
                            Err(ExitStatus::CommandTimedOut.into())
                        }
                    } else {
                        Err(ExitStatus::CommandTimedOut.into())
                    }
                }
                Some(kill_after) => {
                    match wait_or_kill_process(
                        &mut process,
                        &cmd[0],
                        kill_after,
                        preserve_status,
                        foreground,
                        verbose,
                    ) {
                        Ok(status) => Err(status.into()),
                        Err(e) => Err(USimpleError::new(
                            ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into(),
                            e.to_string(),
                        )),
                    }
                }
            }
        }
        Err(_) => {
            send_signal(&mut process, signal, foreground);
            Err(ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into())
        }
    }
}' --new_str '/// Signal handler that forwards termination signals to child processes
unsafe extern "C" fn signal_handler(sig: libc::c_int) {
    // We need to handle the signal and forward it to child processes
    // This is a simplified handler - the actual cleanup happens in the main function
    libc::signal(sig, libc::SIG_DFL);
    libc::raise(sig);
}

/// TODO: Improve exit codes, and make them consistent with the GNU Coreutils exit codes.
fn timeout(
    cmd: &[String],
    duration: Duration,
    signal: usize,
    kill_after: Option<Duration>,
    foreground: bool,
    preserve_status: bool,
    verbose: bool,
) -> UResult<()> {
    // Create a new process group if not in foreground mode
    // This allows us to kill the entire process group when timeout is terminated
    
    if !foreground {
        unsafe { libc::setpgid(0, 0) };
    }
    #[cfg(unix)]
    enable_pipe_errors()?;

    // Spawn the child process
    let mut process = process::Command::new(&cmd[0])
        .args(&cmd[1..])
        .stdin(Stdio::inherit())
        .stdout(Stdio::inherit())
        .stderr(Stdio::inherit())
        .spawn()
        .map_err(|err| {
            let status_code = if err.kind() == ErrorKind::NotFound {
                127
            } else {
                126
            };
            USimpleError::new(
                status_code,
                get_message_with_args(
                    "timeout-error-failed-to-execute-process",
                    HashMap::from([("error".to_string(), err.to_string())]),
                ),
            )
        })?;
    unblock_sigchld();
    
    let child_pid = process.id() as i32;
    
    // Move child to timeout'"'"'s process group if not in foreground mode
    // This ensures signal propagation when timeout is terminated
    if !foreground {
        unsafe {
            libc::setpgid(child_pid, 0);
        }
    }
    
    // Set up signal handlers to forward termination signals to child
    unsafe {
        libc::signal(libc::SIGTERM, signal_handler);
        libc::signal(libc::SIGINT, signal_handler); 
        libc::signal(libc::SIGHUP, signal_handler);
    }
    
    // Wait for the child process for the specified time period
    match process.wait_or_timeout(duration) {
        Ok(Some(status)) => Err(status
            .code()
            .unwrap_or_else(|| preserve_signal_info(status.signal().unwrap()))
            .into()),
        Ok(None) => {
            report_if_verbose(signal, &cmd[0], verbose);
            send_signal(&mut process, signal, foreground);
            match kill_after {
                None => {
                    let status = process.wait()?;
                    if preserve_status {
                        if let Some(ec) = status.code() {
                            Err(ec.into())
                        } else if let Some(sc) = status.signal() {
                            Err(ExitStatus::SignalSent(sc.try_into().unwrap()).into())
                        } else {
                            Err(ExitStatus::CommandTimedOut.into())
                        }
                    } else {
                        Err(ExitStatus::CommandTimedOut.into())
                    }
                }
                Some(kill_after) => {
                    match wait_or_kill_process(
                        &mut process,
                        &cmd[0],
                        kill_after,
                        preserve_status,
                        foreground,
                        verbose,
                    ) {
                        Ok(status) => Err(status.into()),
                        Err(e) => Err(USimpleError::new(
                            ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into(),
                            e.to_string(),
                        )),
                    }
                }
            }
        }
        Err(_) => {
            send_signal(&mut process, signal, foreground);
            Err(ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into())
        }
    }
}'

   395	                        foreground,
   396	                        verbose,
   397	                    ) {
   398	                        Ok(status) => Err(status.into()),
   399	                        Err(e) => Err(USimpleError::new(
   400	                            ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into(),
   401	                            e.to_string(),
   402	                        )),
   403	                    }
   404	                }
   405	            }
   406	        }
   407	        Err(_) => {
   408	            send_signal(&mut process, signal, foreground);
   409	            Err(ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into())
   410	        }
   411	    }
   412	}

The issue persists. The problem is that my signal handler approach is not sufficient to solve the fundamental issue. When timeout receives a SIGTERM signal, it needs to ensure that its child processes are terminated before timeout itself exits.

The key insight I've learned from testing is that GNU timeout properly handles this by ensuring that when it receives a termination signal, it propagates that signal to its child processes. However, my attempts to implement signal handlers and process group management haven't been successful.

Let me implement a more robust solution that properly handles this case. The issue is that when timeout receives a SIGTERM, it needs to:
1. Send the same signal to its child processes
2. Wait for the child processes to terminate
3. Then exit itself

I'll implement this by using a more sophisticated signal handling approach:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/src/uu/timeout/src/timeout.rs   --old_str '/// Signal handler that forwards termination signals to child processes
unsafe extern "C" fn signal_handler(sig: libc::c_int) {
    // We need to handle the signal and forward it to child processes
    // This is a simplified handler - the actual cleanup happens in the main function
    unsafe {
        libc::signal(sig, libc::SIG_DFL);
        libc::raise(sig);
    }
}' --new_str '/// Global variable to store child PID for signal handling
static mut CHILD_PID: i32 = 0;

/// Signal handler that terminates child processes when timeout is terminated
unsafe extern "C" fn signal_handler(sig: libc::c_int) {
    // Forward the signal to the child process group
    if CHILD_PID > 0 {
        // Send signal to the entire process group
        libc::kill(-CHILD_PID, sig);
    }
    
    // Restore default handler and re-raise the signal
    libc::signal(sig, libc::SIG_DFL);
    libc::raise(sig);
}'

2026-01-09 09:14:03,220 - DEBUG - swea-lm - total_tokens_sent=0, total_tokens_received=3,055, total_cost=0.00, total_api_calls=80
2026-01-09 09:14:03,229 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
Looking at the issue and my attempts to fix it, I realize that my approach has been getting increasingly complex without addressing the fundamental problem. Let me step back and implement a proper solution.

The key insight from the PR description is that GNU timeout properly terminates its child processes when it receives a TERM signal, but uutils timeout does not. The issue is that when timeout receives a termination signal, it doesn't propagate that signal to its child processes.

Let me implement a proper fix that actually works:

The fundamental issue is that the current timeout implementation doesn't handle signals properly. When timeout receives a SIGTERM, it needs to:

1. Forward the signal to its child processes
2. Wait for the child processes to terminate
3. Then exit itself

Here's the proper fix:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/src/uu/timeout/src/timeout.rs   --old_str '/// Global variable to store child PID for signal handling
static mut CHILD_PID: i32 = 0;

/// Signal handler that terminates child processes when timeout is terminated
unsafe extern "C" fn signal_handler(sig: libc::c_int) {
    // Forward the signal to the child process group
    unsafe {
        if CHILD_PID > 0 {
            // Send signal to the entire process group
            libc::kill(-CHILD_PID, sig);
        }
        
        // Restore default handler and re-raise the signal
        libc::signal(sig, libc::SIG_DFL);
        libc::raise(sig);
    }
}

/// TODO: Improve exit codes, and make them consistent with the GNU Coreutils exit codes.
fn timeout(
    cmd: &[String],
    duration: Duration,
    signal: usize,
    kill_after: Option<Duration>,
    foreground: bool,
    preserve_status: bool,
    verbose: bool,
) -> UResult<()> {
    // Create a new process group if not in foreground mode
    // This allows us to kill the entire process group when timeout is terminated
    
    if !foreground {
        unsafe { libc::setpgid(0, 0) };
    }
    #[cfg(unix)]
    enable_pipe_errors()?;

    // Spawn the child process
    let mut process = process::Command::new(&cmd[0])
        .args(&cmd[1..])
        .stdin(Stdio::inherit())
        .stdout(Stdio::inherit())
        .stderr(Stdio::inherit())
        .spawn()
        .map_err(|err| {
            let status_code = if err.kind() == ErrorKind::NotFound {
                127
            } else {
                126
            };
            USimpleError::new(
                status_code,
                get_message_with_args(
                    "timeout-error-failed-to-execute-process",
                    HashMap::from([("error".to_string(), err.to_string())]),
                ),
            )
        })?;
    unblock_sigchld();
    
    let child_pid = process.id() as i32;
    
    // Move child to timeout'"'"'s process group if not in foreground mode
    // This ensures signal propagation when timeout is terminated
    if !foreground {
        unsafe {
            libc::setpgid(child_pid, 0);
        }
    }
    
    // Set up signal handlers to forward termination signals to child
    unsafe {
        libc::signal(libc::SIGTERM, signal_handler as libc::sighandler_t);
        libc::signal(libc::SIGINT, signal_handler as libc::sighandler_t); 
        libc::signal(libc::SIGHUP, signal_handler as libc::sighandler_t);
    }
    
    // Wait for the child process for the specified time period

                        } else if let Some(sc) = status.signal() {
                            Err(ExitStatus::SignalSent(sc.try_into().unwrap()).into())
                        } else {

                        }
                    } else {
                        Err(ExitStatus::CommandTimedOut.into())
                    }

                        &mut process,
                        &cmd[0],
                        kill_after,
                        preserve_status,
                        foreground,
                        verbose,

                        Err(e) => Err(USimpleError::new(
                            ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into(),
                            e.to_string(),
                        )),
                    }
                }
            }
        }
        Err(_) => {
            send_signal(&mut process, signal, foreground);
            Err(ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into())
        }

}' --new_str '/// TODO: Improve exit codes, and make them consistent with the GNU Coreutils exit codes.
fn timeout(
    cmd: &[String],
    duration: Duration,
    signal: usize,
    kill_after: Option<Duration>,
    foreground: bool,
    preserve_status: bool,
    verbose: bool,
) -> UResult<()> {
    // Create a new process group if not in foreground mode
    // This allows us to kill the entire process group when timeout is terminated
    if !foreground {
        unsafe { libc::setpgid(0, 0) };
    }
    #[cfg(unix)]
    enable_pipe_errors()?;

    // Spawn the child process
    let mut process = process::Command::new(&cmd[0])
        .args(&cmd[1..])
        .stdin(Stdio::inherit())
        .stdout(Stdio::inherit())
        .stderr(Stdio::inherit())
        .spawn()
        .map_err(|err| {
            let status_code = if err.kind() == ErrorKind::NotFound {
                127
            } else {
                126
            };
            USimpleError::new(
                status_code,
                get_message_with_args(
                    "timeout-error-failed-to-execute-process",
                    HashMap::from([("error".to_string(), err.to_string())]),
                ),
            )
        })?;
    unblock_sigchld();
    
    let child_pid = process.id() as i32;
    
    // Move child to timeout'"'"'s process group if not in foreground mode
    // This ensures signal propagation when timeout is terminated
    if !foreground {
        unsafe {
            libc::setpgid(child_pid, 0);
        }
    }
    
    // Wait for the child process for the specified time period
    match process.wait_or_timeout(duration) {
        Ok(Some(status)) => Err(status
            .code()
            .unwrap_or_else(|| preserve_signal_info(status.signal().unwrap()))
            .into()),
        Ok(None) => {
            report_if_verbose(signal, &cmd[0], verbose);
            send_signal(&mut process, signal, foreground);
            match kill_after {
                None => {
                    let status = process.wait()?;
                    if preserve_status {
                        if let Some(ec) = status.code() {
                            Err(ec.into())
                        } else if let Some(sc) = status.signal() {
                            Err(ExitStatus::SignalSent(sc.try_into().unwrap()).into())
                        } else {
                            Err(ExitStatus::CommandTimedOut.into())
                        }
                    } else {
                        Err(ExitStatus::CommandTimedOut.into())
                    }
                }
                Some(kill_after) => {
                    match wait_or_kill_process(
                        &mut process,
                        &cmd[0],
                        kill_after,
                        preserve_status,
                        foreground,
                        verbose,
                    ) {
                        Ok(status) => Err(status.into()),
                        Err(e) => Err(USimpleError::new(
                            ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into(),
                            e.to_string(),
                        )),
                    }
                }
            }
        }
        Err(_) => {
            send_signal(&mut process, signal, foreground);
            Err(ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into())
        }
    }

After analyzing the code and the issue, I realize that my previous attempts were becoming overly complex without addressing the fundamental problem. Let me implement a proper, minimal fix that addresses the core issue described in the PR.

The key problem is that when the `timeout` utility receives a TERM signal, it doesn't properly propagate that signal to its child processes before exiting. This causes the child processes to become orphans and continue running, which is the behavior described in the PR.

The fundamental issue is that the current implementation doesn't handle termination signals properly. When timeout receives a SIGTERM, it needs to ensure that its child processes are terminated first.

Let me implement the correct fix:

}' --new_str '/// TODO: Improve exit codes, and make them consistent with the GNU Coreutils exit codes.
fn timeout(
    cmd: &[String],
    duration: Duration,
    signal: usize,
    kill_after: Option<Duration>,
    foreground: bool,
    preserve_status: bool,
    verbose: bool,
) -> UResult<()> {
    // Create a new process group if not in foreground mode
    // This allows us to kill the entire process group when timeout is terminated
    if !foreground {
        unsafe { libc::setpgid(0, 0) };
    }
    #[cfg(unix)]
    enable_pipe_errors()?;

    // Spawn the child process
    let mut process = process::Command::new(&cmd[0])
        .args(&cmd[1..])
        .stdin(Stdio::inherit())
        .stdout(Stdio::inherit())
        .stderr(Stdio::inherit())
        .spawn()
        .map_err(|err| {
            let status_code = if err.kind() == ErrorKind::NotFound {
                127
            } else {
                126
            };
            USimpleError::new(
                status_code,
                get_message_with_args(
                    "timeout-error-failed-to-execute-process",
                    HashMap::from([("error".to_string(), err.to_string())]),
                ),
            )
        })?;
    unblock_sigchld();
    
    let child_pid = process.id() as i32;
    
    // Move child to timeout'"'"'s process group if not in foreground mode
    // This ensures signal propagation when timeout is terminated
    if !foreground {
        unsafe {
            libc::setpgid(child_pid, 0);
        }
    }
    
    // Set up signal handlers to ensure child processes are terminated when timeout is terminated
    unsafe {
        // SIGTERM handler that kills the child process group before exiting
        extern "C" fn sigterm_handler(sig: libc::c_int) {
            unsafe {
                // Kill the entire process group (negative PID means process group)
                libc::kill(0, sig);
                // Restore default handler and re-raise the signal
                libc::signal(sig, libc::SIG_DFL);
                libc::raise(sig);
            }
        }
        
        libc::signal(libc::SIGTERM, sigterm_handler as libc::sighandler_t);
        libc::signal(libc::SIGINT, sigterm_handler as libc::sighandler_t);
    }
    
    // Wait for the child process for the specified time period
    match process.wait_or_timeout(duration) {
        Ok(Some(status)) => Err(status
            .code()
            .unwrap_or_else(|| preserve_signal_info(status.signal().unwrap()))
            .into()),
        Ok(None) => {
            report_if_verbose(signal, &cmd[0], verbose);
            send_signal(&mut process, signal, foreground);
            match kill_after {
                None => {
                    let status = process.wait()?;
                    if preserve_status {
                        if let Some(ec) = status.code() {
                            Err(ec.into())
                        } else if let Some(sc) = status.signal() {
                            Err(ExitStatus::SignalSent(sc.try_into().unwrap()).into())
                        } else {
                            Err(ExitStatus::CommandTimedOut.into())
                        }
                    } else {
                        Err(ExitStatus::CommandTimedOut.into())
                    }
                }
                Some(kill_after) => {
                    match wait_or_kill_process(
                        &mut process,
                        &cmd[0],
                        kill_after,
                        preserve_status,
                        foreground,
                        verbose,
                    ) {
                        Ok(status) => Err(status.into()),
                        Err(e) => Err(USimpleError::new(
                            ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into(),
                            e.to_string(),
                        )),
                    }
                }
            }
        }
        Err(_) => {
            send_signal(&mut process, signal, foreground);
            Err(ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into())
        }
    }

   293	fn preserve_signal_info(signal: libc::c_int) -> libc::c_int {
   294	    // Do nothing
   295	    signal
   296	}
   297	
   298	/// TODO: Improve exit codes, and make them consistent with the GNU Coreutils exit codes.
   299	fn timeout(
   300	    cmd: &[String],
   301	    duration: Duration,
   302	    signal: usize,
   303	    kill_after: Option<Duration>,
   304	    foreground: bool,
   305	    preserve_status: bool,
   306	    verbose: bool,
   307	) -> UResult<()> {
   308	    // Create a new process group if not in foreground mode
   309	    // This allows us to kill the entire process group when timeout is terminated
   310	    if !foreground {
   311	        unsafe { libc::setpgid(0, 0) };
   312	    }
   313	    #[cfg(unix)]
   314	    enable_pipe_errors()?;
   315	
   316	    // Spawn the child process
   317	    let mut process = process::Command::new(&cmd[0])
   318	        .args(&cmd[1..])
   319	        .stdin(Stdio::inherit())
   320	        .stdout(Stdio::inherit())
   321	        .stderr(Stdio::inherit())
   322	        .spawn()
   323	        .map_err(|err| {
   324	            let status_code = if err.kind() == ErrorKind::NotFound {
   325	                127
   326	            } else {
   327	                126
   328	            };
   329	            USimpleError::new(
   330	                status_code,
   331	                get_message_with_args(
   332	                    "timeout-error-failed-to-execute-process",
   333	                    HashMap::from([("error".to_string(), err.to_string())]),
   334	                ),
   335	            )
   336	        })?;
   337	    unblock_sigchld();
   338	    
   339	    let child_pid = process.id() as i32;
   340	    
   341	    // Move child to timeout's process group if not in foreground mode
   342	    // This ensures signal propagation when timeout is terminated
   343	    if !foreground {
   344	        unsafe {
   345	            libc::setpgid(child_pid, 0);
   346	        }
   347	    }
   348	    
   349	    // Set up signal handlers to ensure child processes are terminated when timeout is terminated
   350	    unsafe {
   351	        // SIGTERM handler that kills the child process group before exiting
   352	        extern "C" fn sigterm_handler(sig: libc::c_int) {
   353	            unsafe {
   354	                // Kill the entire process group (negative PID means process group)
   355	                libc::kill(0, sig);
   356	                // Restore default handler and re-raise the signal
   357	                libc::signal(sig, libc::SIG_DFL);
   358	                libc::raise(sig);
   359	            }
   360	        }
   361	        
   362	        libc::signal(libc::SIGTERM, sigterm_handler as libc::sighandler_t);
   363	        libc::signal(libc::SIGINT, sigterm_handler as libc::sighandler_t);
   364	    }
   365	    
   366	    // Wait for the child process for the specified time period
   367	    match process.wait_or_timeout(duration) {
   368	        Ok(Some(status)) => Err(status
   369	            .code()
   370	            .unwrap_or_else(|| preserve_signal_info(status.signal().unwrap()))
   371	            .into()),
   372	        Ok(None) => {
   373	            report_if_verbose(signal, &cmd[0], verbose);
   374	            send_signal(&mut process, signal, foreground);
   375	            match kill_after {
   376	                None => {
   377	                    let status = process.wait()?;
   378	                    if preserve_status {
   379	                        if let Some(ec) = status.code() {
   380	                            Err(ec.into())
   381	                        } else if let Some(sc) = status.signal() {
   382	                            Err(ExitStatus::SignalSent(sc.try_into().unwrap()).into())
   383	                        } else {
   384	                            Err(ExitStatus::CommandTimedOut.into())
   385	                        }
   386	                    } else {
   387	                        Err(ExitStatus::CommandTimedOut.into())
   388	                    }
   389	                }
   390	                Some(kill_after) => {
   391	                    match wait_or_kill_process(
   392	                        &mut process,
   393	                        &cmd[0],
   394	                        kill_after,
   395	                        preserve_status,
   396	                        foreground,
   397	                        verbose,
   398	                    ) {
   399	                        Ok(status) => Err(status.into()),
   400	                        Err(e) => Err(USimpleError::new(
   401	                            ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into(),
   402	                            e.to_string(),
   403	                        )),
   404	                    }
   405	                }
   406	            }
   407	        }
   408	        Err(_) => {
   409	            send_signal(&mut process, signal, foreground);
   410	            Err(ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into())
   411	        }
   412	    }
   413	}

+#!/usr/bin/env python3
+import os
+import subprocess
+import time
+import signal
+import sys
+
+def test_timeout_signal_handling():
+    """Test if timeout properly terminates child process when receiving TERM signal"""
+    
+    # Build the timeout utility first
+    print("Building timeout utility...")
+    build_result = subprocess.run(['cargo', 'build', '--features', 'timeout'], 
+                                 cwd='/testbed', capture_output=True, text=True)
+    if build_result.returncode != 0:
+        print(f"Build failed: {build_result.stderr}")
+        return False
+    
+    # Start timeout with a long-running command (sleep 60)
+    print("Starting timeout with sleep 60...")
+    timeout_proc = subprocess.Popen(['/testbed/target/debug/timeout', '60', 'sleep', '60'], 
+                                   stdout=subprocess.PIPE, stderr=subprocess.PIPE)
+    
+    # Give it a moment to start
+    time.sleep(1)
+    
+    # Find the child sleep process using ps
+    sleep_pid = None
+    parent_pid = timeout_proc.pid
+    
+    ps_result = subprocess.run(['ps', '-o', 'pid,ppid,comm', '-A'], 
+                              capture_output=True, text=True)
+    
+    for line in ps_result.stdout.splitlines():
+        parts = line.strip().split()
+        if len(parts) >= 3:
+            pid, ppid, comm = parts[0], parts[1], parts[2]
+            if ppid == str(parent_pid) and comm == 'sleep':
+                sleep_pid = int(pid)
+                print(f"Found child sleep process: PID {sleep_pid}")
+                break
+    
+    if sleep_pid is None:
+        print("ERROR: Could not find child sleep process")
+        timeout_proc.terminate()
+        return False
+    
+    # Send TERM signal to timeout process
+    print(f"Sending TERM signal to timeout process (PID {parent_pid})...")
+    timeout_proc.terminate()
+    
+    # Wait for timeout process to terminate
+    try:
+        timeout_proc.wait(timeout=5)
+        print("Timeout process terminated")
+    except subprocess.TimeoutExpired:
+        print("Timeout process did not terminate within 5 seconds")
+        timeout_proc.kill()
+    
+    # Check if child sleep process is still running
+    time.sleep(1)  # Give it a moment to propagate
+    
+    # Check if the sleep process is still running
+    check_result = subprocess.run(['ps', '-p', str(sleep_pid)], 
+                                 capture_output=True, text=True)
+    
+    if check_result.returncode == 0:
+        # Process is still running, get its new parent
+        ps_result = subprocess.run(['ps', '-o', 'ppid', '-p', str(sleep_pid)], 
+                                  capture_output=True, text=True)
+        new_ppid = None
+        for line in ps_result.stdout.splitlines():
+            if line.strip().isdigit():
+                new_ppid = line.strip()
+                break
+        
+        print(f"ERROR: Child sleep process (PID {sleep_pid}) is still running!")
+        print(f"New parent PID: {new_ppid}")
+        
+        # Clean up the leftover process
+        print("Cleaning up leftover child process...")
+        subprocess.run(['kill', str(sleep_pid)])
+        return False
+    else:
+        print(f"SUCCESS: Child sleep process (PID {sleep_pid}) terminated properly")
+        return True
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    success = test_timeout_signal_handling()
+    sys.exit(0 if success else 1)

diff --git a/test_simple.sh b/test_simple.sh
new file mode 100755
index 000000000..f31d520c9
--- /dev/null
+++ b/test_simple.sh
@@ -0,0 +1,90 @@
+#!/bin/bash
+
+# Simple test to verify the timeout behavior
+
+# Build coreutils
+echo "Building coreutils..."
+cargo build --features timeout
+
+# Test 1: Run timeout in the background (non-foreground mode by default)
+echo "Test 1: Running timeout 10 sleep 60 in background..."
+./target/debug/coreutils timeout 10 sleep 60 &
+TIMEOUT_PID=$!
+sleep 1
+
+# Find the sleep process
+SLEEP_PID=$(ps -o pid,ppid,comm -A | awk -v ppid=$TIMEOUT_PID '$2 == ppid && $3 == "sleep" {print $1}')
+if [ -z "$SLEEP_PID" ]; then
+    echo "ERROR: Could not find child sleep process"
+    kill $TIMEOUT_PID
+    exit 1
+fi
+
+echo "Timeout PID: $TIMEOUT_PID, Sleep PID: $SLEEP_PID"
+
+# Check the process groups
+TIMEOUT_PGRP=$(ps -o pgid -p $TIMEOUT_PID | tail -1)
+SLEEP_PGRP=$(ps -o pgid -p $SLEEP_PID | tail -1)
+echo "Timeout PGID: $TIMEOUT_PGRP, Sleep PGID: $SLEEP_PGRP"
+
+# Send TERM signal to timeout
+echo "Sending TERM to timeout..."
+kill $TIMEOUT_PID
+sleep 1
+
+# Check if processes are still running
+if ps -p $TIMEOUT_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
+    echo "Timeout still running"
+    kill -9 $TIMEOUT_PID
+else
+    echo "Timeout terminated"
+fi
+
+if ps -p $SLEEP_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
+    NEW_PPID=$(ps -o ppid -p $SLEEP_PID | tail -1)
+    echo "ERROR: Sleep process still running! New PPID: $NEW_PPID"
+    kill $SLEEP_PID
+else
+    echo "SUCCESS: Sleep process terminated"
+fi
+
+echo ""
+echo "Test 2: Testing GNU timeout for comparison..."
+/usr/bin/timeout 10 sleep 60 &
+GNU_TIMEOUT_PID=$!
+sleep 1
+
+GNU_SLEEP_PID=$(ps -o pid,ppid,comm -A | awk -v ppid=$GNU_TIMEOUT_PID '$2 == ppid && $3 == "sleep" {print $1}')
+if [ -z "$GNU_SLEEP_PID" ]; then
+    echo "ERROR: Could not find GNU timeout child sleep process"
+    kill $GNU_TIMEOUT_PID
+    exit 1
+fi
+
+echo "GNU Timeout PID: $GNU_TIMEOUT_PID, Sleep PID: $GNU_SLEEP_PID"
+
+# Check GNU timeout process groups
+GNU_TIMEOUT_PGRP=$(ps -o pgid -p $GNU_TIMEOUT_PID | tail -1)
+GNU_SLEEP_PGRP=$(ps -o pgid -p $GNU_SLEEP_PID | tail -1)
+echo "GNU Timeout PGID: $GNU_TIMEOUT_PGRP, Sleep PGID: $GNU_SLEEP_PGRP"
+
+# Send TERM signal to GNU timeout
+echo "Sending TERM to GNU timeout..."
+kill $GNU_TIMEOUT_PID
+sleep 1
+
+# Check if GNU timeout processes are still running
+if ps -p $GNU_TIMEOUT_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
+    echo "GNU timeout still running"
+    kill -9 $GNU_TIMEOUT_PID
+else
+    echo "GNU timeout terminated"
+fi
+
+if ps -p $GNU_SLEEP_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
+    NEW_PPID=$(ps -o ppid -p $GNU_SLEEP_PID | tail -1)
+    echo "ERROR: GNU timeout sleep process still running! New PPID: $NEW_PPID"
+    kill $GNU_SLEEP_PID
+else
+    echo "SUCCESS: GNU timeout sleep process terminated"
+fi

diff --git a/test_timeout.sh b/test_timeout.sh
new file mode 100755
index 000000000..f627ff4a9
--- /dev/null
+++ b/test_timeout.sh
@@ -0,0 +1,53 @@
+#!/bin/bash
+
+# Build coreutils if needed
+echo "Building coreutils..."
+cargo build --features timeout
+
+# Test the timeout utility with a simple test
+echo "Testing timeout utility..."
+
+# Start timeout with sleep
+./target/debug/coreutils timeout 10 sleep 60 &
+TIMEOUT_PID=$!
+
+echo "Timeout process started with PID: $TIMEOUT_PID"
+
+# Wait a moment then find the sleep child process
+sleep 1
+
+SLEEP_PID=$(ps -o pid,ppid,comm -A | awk -v ppid=$TIMEOUT_PID '$2 == ppid && $3 == "sleep" {print $1}')
+if [ -z "$SLEEP_PID" ]; then
+    echo "ERROR: Could not find child sleep process"
+    kill $TIMEOUT_PID
+    exit 1
+fi
+
+echo "Found child sleep process with PID: $SLEEP_PID"
+
+# Send TERM signal to timeout process
+echo "Sending TERM signal to timeout process (PID: $TIMEOUT_PID)..."
+kill $TIMEOUT_PID
+
+# Wait for timeout to terminate
+sleep 2
+
+# Check if timeout process terminated
+if ps -p $TIMEOUT_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
+    echo "Timeout process still running, killing it..."
+    kill -9 $TIMEOUT_PID
+fi
+
+# Check if child sleep process is still running
+if ps -p $SLEEP_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
+    NEW_PPID=$(ps -o ppid -p $SLEEP_PID | tail -1)
+    echo "ERROR: Child sleep process (PID: $SLEEP_PID) is still running!"
+    echo "New parent PID: $NEW_PPID"
+    
+    # Clean up
+    kill $SLEEP_PID
+    exit 1
+else
+    echo "SUCCESS: Child sleep process terminated properly"
+    exit 0
+fi
\ No newline at end of file

</diff>
